<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch4 — T2 findings for Healing wholeness through faith exercised -->

**T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries**

- *T2.10.1* — _Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other direction…_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, a clear downward-then-manifesting movement is evidenced. Interior faith (formed at the heart/soul level) moves outward through the body (the touch of the garment, the cry of Bartimaeus) and occasions a physical healing, which then feeds back into the soul as peace (Mar 5:34, Luk 8:48) or into restored relational posture (Mar 10:52, discipleship following). In Jam 5:15 and 1Pe 3:21 the movement extends further: from intercessory faith (inner being of intercessor) → prayer (speech act) → healing of body → cleansing of conscience (inner being of the sick). The constitutional movement thus runs: soul/heart → bodily act → bodily healing → soul/conscience restored — a multi-level circuit.
- *T2.10.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The sequence evidenced across M38-C VCG-01 and VCG-02 follows a consistent four-stage pattern: (1) *Formation*: interior faith/conviction arises in the heart or conscience of the seeker (Mat 9:21, Mar 5:28, Mar 5:23, Luk 8:50). (2) *Expression*: faith moves through the body — touch, cry, prostration, prayer (Mar 5:28, Mar 10:47, Luk 17:16, Jam 5:15). (3) *Reception*: sōzō descends as physical restoration (Mat 9:22, Mar 5:34, Mar 10:52, etc.). (4) *Consolidation*: the inner being is confirmed in peace, discipleship, or cleansed conscience (Mar 5:34 "go in peace"; Mar 10:52 "followed Jesus"; 1Pe 3:21 "good conscience"). VCG-02 compresses stages 1–2 into a crisis posture where fear and faith co-exist before the sōzō word arrives. The pattern is consistent and directional, not reversible.
- *T2.10.3* — _If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Constitutional movement is positively evidenced. See T2.10.1 and T2.10.2. The four-stage sequence (formation → expression → reception → consolidation) is documented and directional. No silence note is required.
- *T2.2.1* — _Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The evidence locates the characteristic at the soul level indirectly but substantially. Mar 5:28 (vc_id=9013) describes the hemorrhaging woman's "inner conviction" operating before any outward act, placing faith in the inward personal faculty. Mat 9:21 (vc_id=9010) presents the woman's interior faith-speech ("if I touch his garment I will be made well") as a soul-level self-persuasion. Luk 8:48 (vc_id=9017) and Mar 5:34 (vc_id=9014) confirm that the resultant "peace" is granted to the inner person. Jam 5:15 (vc_id=9024) names conscience as the organ restored, and 1Pe 3:21 (vc_id=8992) grounds salvation in an interior appeal (eperōtēma) to God for a good conscience — both pointing to soul-level location. The characteristic's primary locus is the interior personal faculty of faith and conscience.
- *T2.2.2* — _What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Soul-level location reveals that faith exercised as healing-wholeness is a deeply *personal and interior* event. The woman's pre-touch inner monologue (Mat 9:21, vc_id=9010; Mar 5:28, vc_id=9013) shows that the activating conviction is formed in the inmost personal register before any observable act. Peace granted after healing (Mar 5:34, Luk 8:48) confirms that the soul — not only the body — is the ultimate beneficiary. In 1Pe 3:21 and Jam 5:15 conscience is the inmost organ that salvation touches and clears, indicating that the characteristic's deepest reach is the personal interior. Soul-level location thus reveals this characteristic as irreducibly interior: physical healing is the outward sign of an inner transformation.
- *T2.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Evidence is not silent: soul-level location is positively evidenced. See T2.2.1 and T2.2.2. Faith as the interior activating faculty, conscience as the inner organ restored, and peace as the inward state granted — all locate the characteristic firmly at the soul level. No silence note is required.
- *T2.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Heart-location is implied rather than lexically explicit across M38-C. Mar 5:28 (vc_id=9013) is glossed as "faith working in the heart before any word is spoken," placing interior conviction in the heart. Mat 9:21–22 (vc_id=9010–9011) show an interior faith-speech and its confirmation — faith operating at the level of deepest personal trust, which the corpus's own meanings describe as "heart trusting" (kw on vc_id=9011, 9013). The heart is thus the implied seat of the activating faith, though no verse in this VCG set uses the word kardia explicitly to name that location.
- *T2.3.2* — _What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this…_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Heart-location, where evidenced (Mar 5:28, vc_id=9013; Mat 9:21–22, vc_id=9010–9011), reveals that faith-activated healing engages the *integrating and trusting* function of the heart. The keyword "heart trusting" on vc_id=9011 and 9013 indicates that the heart's trust-capacity is the specific sub-function operative here — not merely cognitive assent or emotional feeling, but a settled orientation of personal reliance directed toward Jesus. This pre-verbal, pre-action conviction ("before any word is spoken," Mar 5:28 gloss) shows the heart operating as the source of determination and will, integrating knowing ("if I touch his garment"), willing (she presses through the crowd), and confident expectation (she will be made well).
- *T2.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Evidence is not silent: heart-location is implied and supported by the corpus meanings. See T2.3.1 and T2.3.2. The keywords "heart trusting" (vc_id=9011, 9013) and the gloss "faith working in the heart before any word is spoken" (vc_id=9013) together establish heart as the implied seat of this characteristic. No silence note is required.
- *T2.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence surface any soul-level location beyond heart and mind for this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes. Two soul-level sub-faculties beyond heart and mind appear. First, *conscience* is explicitly named: 1Pe 3:21 (vc_id=8992) defines baptism's saving efficacy as "an appeal to God for a good conscience," and Jam 5:15 (vc_id=9024) pairs healing of body with forgiveness/cleansing of sin, implicating conscience as the inward register of that forgiveness. Second, *urgency / desperate will* appears in VCG-02: Mar 5:23 (vc_id=9012) locates an inner-being posture of anguished parental longing ("earnest faith and parental love seeking life"), and Luk 8:50 (vc_id=9018) identifies fear as the inner-being state that faith displaces — marking the affective-volitional sub-region of the soul as active in this characteristic.
- *T2.5.2* — _If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Two sub-locations were identified in T2.5.1: *conscience* and the *affective-volitional* sub-region. Conscience (1Pe 3:21, vc_id=8992; Jam 5:15, vc_id=9024) reveals that the characteristic's ultimate inner-being reach is moral and relational standing before God: sōzō is not complete until the conscience is addressed. This distinguishes M38-C from mere physical cure. The affective-volitional sub-region (Mar 5:23, vc_id=9012; Luk 8:50, vc_id=9018) — urgent parental love and fear displaced by faith — reveals that the characteristic can be activated under conditions of mortal crisis, where the soul's affective register (grief, fear, love) is the presenting inner-being posture that faith must overcome or redirect. Taken together, these locations reveal that the characteristic spans the full affective-moral range of the soul.
- *T2.5.3* — _If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Evidence is not silent: conscience and the affective-volitional sub-region are both positively evidenced as soul sub-locations for this characteristic. See T2.5.1 and T2.5.2. No silence note is required.
- *T2.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, with specific textual warrants. The hemorrhaging woman's touch of Jesus's garment (Mar 5:28, vc_id=9013; Mat 9:21, vc_id=9010) makes the *hand* and the act of physical contact the concrete medium through which interior faith reaches toward sōzō. Bartimaeus's restored *eyes* (Mar 10:52, vc_id=9016; Luk 18:42, vc_id=9020) and the blind man's sight-restoration make the visual organ the explicit site of healing. The Samaritan leper's cleansed *skin* (Luk 17:19, vc_id=9019) and the dying girl's restoration to life (Mar 5:23, vc_id=9012; Luk 8:50, vc_id=9018) extend the body-part linkage to skin and the whole living body. In Jam 5:15 the "sick" person's body is the named site of the prayer of faith's effect.
- *T2.6.2* — _If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Scripture's body-part linkages in M38-C are primarily *mediating* and *confirmatory*. The touch of the garment (Mar 5:28, Mat 9:21) is a *mediating* act: the physical contact is the vehicle through which interior faith reaches its object, not the cause of healing. Jesus's question "who touched me?" (Mar 5:30, context of vc_id=9013) confirms that the body-act is the medium, not the source. The restored eyes (Mar 10:52, Luk 18:42) and cleansed skin (Luk 17:19) are *confirmatory* and *expressive*: they make the inner sōzō visible and publicly attestable. In Jam 5:15 the sick body is the *occasion* for a prayer that also addresses the soul — the body-link is therefore *indicative* of a deeper need. Scripture's use of body parts here consistently frames them as witnesses or channels of an inward reality, not autonomous sites of saving power.
- *T2.6.3* — _If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Body-part links are positively evidenced. See T2.6.1 and T2.6.2. No silence note is required.
- *T2.7.1* — _Where a body-characteristic link exists, which direction does it run — does the soul express through the body, does the body feed back to th…_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The primary direction is *soul/heart-to-body*: interior faith (formed in the heart before any word is spoken, Mar 5:28, vc_id=9013) activates the healing of the physical organ. Jesus consistently names faith as the causal factor operating from within the person outward ("your faith has made you well," Mat 9:22, vc_id=9011; Mar 5:34, vc_id=9014; Mar 10:52, vc_id=9016; Luk 8:48, vc_id=9017; Luk 17:19, vc_id=9019; Luk 18:42, vc_id=9020). However, a secondary *body-to-soul feedback* is present: the physical act of touch (Mar 5:28), the act of crying out (Mar 10:52), and the physical return/prostration of the Samaritan (Luk 17:19) are bodily expressions that accompany and complete the soul's movement — suggesting bidirectional interaction rather than a purely one-way flow.
- *T2.7.2* — _What is the consequence of that directionality for understanding the characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The primary soul-to-body direction, with secondary body-to-soul feedback (established in T2.7.1), has two consequences for understanding the characteristic. First, it confirms that the inner being (faith, heart-trust) is genuinely *causal* and not merely accompanying — Jesus's attribution formula ("your faith has made you well," six times across the synoptics) makes inner faith the named operative cause, not the bodily act. Second, the bodily expression of faith (touch, cry, prostration) is not incidental but functionally *completing*: it is the point at which interior conviction becomes directed action, which itself opens the circuit of sōzō. This means the characteristic is neither purely inner (quietist) nor purely outer (ritualist) but constitutionally integrated, requiring the soul-body axis to be engaged for the full healing-wholeness event to occur.
- *T2.7.3* — _If no body-characteristic link is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — A body-characteristic link is positively evidenced with clear directionality. See T2.7.1 and T2.7.2. No silence note is required.
- *T2.9.1* — _Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, …_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The evidence points to a *convergent* origin. On the human side, faith is formed within the person — the woman's interior conviction pre-exists Jesus's word (Mat 9:21, Mar 5:28), and Bartimaeus's persistent cry arises from within himself. On the divine side, the saving act is explicitly attributed to Christ's power (sōzō named in every anchor verse) and, in Jam 5:15 (vc_id=9024), to God who heals through the prayer of faith. In 1Pe 3:21 (vc_id=8992) the appeal is directed *to* God through Christ's resurrection, grounding the saving act in divine agency. The characteristic therefore originates at the intersection of internally-generated faith and externally-bestowed divine power — neither purely from within the person nor purely imposed from outside.
- *T2.9.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The evidence reveals a *dual* origin structure. (1) Human interior: faith is formed within the person's own inner being prior to any external prompting in most M38-C cases (Mat 9:21, Mar 5:28, Mar 10:46–47). The woman's interior monologue and Bartimaeus's self-initiated cry both represent faith generated from within. (2) Divine enabling: the actual sōzō event is always attributed to Christ's power, and in Jam 5:15 and 1Pe 3:21 the saving/healing is explicitly God's act in response to faith. These two origins are not competitive; the corpus presents them as structurally necessary to each other — faith without the divine respondent is inert, and divine power here is consistently accessed through faith as the activating human contribution. The origin is therefore irreducibly dual.
- *T2.9.3* — _Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Partial variation is observable. In VCG-01 (individual healing narratives), faith originates within the seeking person (interior monologue, persistent cry) and the divine response is immediate and personal. In VCG-02 (crisis/death context, vc_id=9012, 9018), faith is commanded from outside by Jesus ("only believe"), introducing an element of externally-prompted origin not present in VCG-01. In VCG-03 (Jam 5:15, 1Pe 3:21), the origin shifts further: faith is exercised corporately (intercessory prayer by elders) or mediated through a rite (baptism), suggesting that in communal/ecclesial contexts the characteristic's origin is partly institutional and partly inward. The dual structure (human faith + divine power) remains constant, but the *trigger* of faith shifts from spontaneous interior conviction to commanded belief to mediated corporate intercession across the three VCGs.
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch4 — T2 silences for Healing wholeness through faith exercised -->

**T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries**

- *T2.1.1* — _Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — The twelve verses in M38-C (VCG-01, VCG-02, VCG-03) do not explicitly assign this characteristic to the *spirit* level by name. No verse uses pneuma to locate faith or healing-wholeness at the spirit stratum. The operative faculty named throughout is faith (pistis), and the locus described is the heart and conscience (Mar 5:28 "inner conviction"; Jam 5:15 "prayer of faith"; 1Pe 3:21 "appeal to God for a good conscience"). Spirit-level location as a distinct anatomical register is not affirmed in this corpus.
- *T2.1.2* — _Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — The evidence does not indicate that the characteristic originates primarily at the spirit level. The named operative faculty is faith exercised within the human interior (heart, conscience, inner conviction), and the saving source is Christ/God acting from outside. No verse in M38-C deploys pneuma or explicitly assigns the origin of faith-activated healing to the human spirit stratum.
- *T2.1.3* — _What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — Since spirit-level location is not evidenced for this characteristic in M38-C (see T2.1.1 and T2.1.2), no finding can be drawn about what such location would reveal. The depth and nature of the characteristic is instead evidenced at the soul level (heart, conscience, faith-faculty) as documented in T2.2.1 and T2.5.1.
- *T2.1.4* — _If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location for this characteristic. No verse in M38-C assigns faith-activated healing-wholeness to the human spirit (pneuma) as a distinct constitutional stratum. This silence is noted explicitly.
- *T2.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — No verse in M38-C explicitly locates this characteristic in the mind (nous, dianoia, or phronēma). The operative faculty throughout is faith (pistis) and conscience (syneidēsis in 1Pe 3:21). The woman's inner faith-speech (Mat 9:21, Mar 5:28) might carry a cognitive colouration, but the corpus meanings do not assign it to the mind faculty. Mind-level location is not evidenced.
- *T2.4.2* — _What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — Since mind-level location is not evidenced in this corpus (see T2.4.1), no finding can be drawn from it. The characteristic does not appear to operate primarily through the discursive or analytical functions of the mind. This silence may itself be significant: faith-activated healing in M38-C precedes verbal articulation and rational deliberation, suggesting the characteristic's operative core is sub-cognitive.
- *T2.4.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mind-location, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — The evidence is silent on mind-level location. No verse in M38-C assigns the characteristic to nous, dianoia, or any explicit mind-faculty. The characteristic's inner-being locus is the heart and conscience, not the discursive or analytical mind. This silence is noted explicitly.
- *T2.8.1* — _Does sustained operation of this characteristic leave a constitutional deposit in the body or its design — including DNA or generational con…_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — The corpus is silent on any sustained constitutional deposit, generational consequence, or DNA-level effect. The healings in M38-C are discrete salvific events rather than ongoing practices whose cumulative effect is described. No verse addresses whether repeated exercise of faith-activated healing leaves a lasting constitutional imprint. This finding feeds into T5.7.
- *T2.8.2* — _What evidence supports or contradicts this?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — No evidence in M38-C addresses whether sustained or repeated exercise of faith-activated healing leaves a constitutional deposit in the body. The corpus records discrete healing events. No verse describes cumulative bodily change, altered physical constitution, generational blessing, or heritable transformation resulting from the characteristic. The silence is consistent and complete. This finding feeds into T5.7.
- *T2.8.3* — _If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly. This finding feeds directly into T5.7._
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — The evidence is silent on constitutional deposit in the body. No verse in M38-C describes any lasting bodily imprint, generational consequence, or cumulative constitutional change resulting from the sustained exercise of faith-activated healing. This silence is noted explicitly and feeds into T5.7.
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch4 — T3 findings for Healing wholeness through faith exercised -->

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.1.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual disce…_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, with a specific inner-sense register. The woman's pre-touch interior speech (Mat 9:21, vc_id=9010; Mar 5:28, vc_id=9013) shows an interior *perception* of Jesus's healing capacity — a knowing by apprehension that precedes rational argument. Bartimaeus's repeated cry "Son of David, have mercy on me" (context of Mar 10:52, vc_id=9016) presupposes a spiritual perception that Jesus is the Messianic healer. The Samaritan leper's return (Luk 17:19, vc_id=9019) presupposes perception that his healing is not random but sourced in Jesus. The operative inner sense is not physical sight (paradoxically, several healees are blind or touch-mediated) but a form of *spiritual discernment* — an inner apprehension of Jesus's identity and salvific power that makes faith possible.
- *T3.1.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic primarily *enables and deepens* spiritual perception. In the individual healing narratives, the faith-seekers already possess a perceptive grasp of Jesus's identity before the healing event; the healing deepens that perception retroactively (the Samaritan sees Jesus differently after his cleansing; Bartimaeus follows Jesus with open eyes). In Luk 8:50 (vc_id=9018), Jesus's command "only believe" works *against* the perceptive report (the girl is dead) — faith here partially *bypasses* the evidence of physical perception in favour of spiritual discernment. This suggests that when fear-driven perception of mortal reality threatens faith, the characteristic holds the spiritual perception in tension with and priority over the physical. The characteristic does not impair perception but reorders its authority.
- *T3.1.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The pattern of perception engagement in M38-C reveals that this characteristic is *trans-sensory* in its perceptive requirement. The faith-healings consistently involve persons whose physical perception is compromised (blind Bartimaeus, vc_id=9016, 9020; the hemorrhaging woman who cannot see the source of power, vc_id=9013) or irrelevant (leper, dying child), yet whose inner spiritual perception is highly active. This inverse pattern — physical sense impaired or bypassed, spiritual apprehension operative — reveals that faith-activated healing-wholeness depends on and exercises an *inner* perceptive faculty (discernment of Jesus's identity and power) that is independent of, and in some cases prior to, restored physical perception. The characteristic therefore reveals that the deepest perceptive capacity is not sensory but relational-spiritual.
- *T3.10.1* — _Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, though partially. Conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — appears most clearly in the act of returning to give thanks (Luk 17:19, vc_id=9019, kw: 'gratitude'): the Samaritan leper's return is a conscientious act that combines moral awareness (recognition of benefit received), volition (choosing to return), and action (prostrating himself before Jesus). The elders' intercessory prayer in Jam 5:15 similarly integrates moral awareness (concern for sin's possible role in illness), volition (choosing to pray), and action (anointing and praying). The characteristic thus engages conscientiousness at the response-to-sōzō stage rather than the initiating stage — it is the conscientious person who completes the wholeness circuit through grateful, responsive action.
- *T3.10.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic *enables and expresses* conscientiousness. The Samaritan leper's return in Luk 17:19 (vc_id=9019) is the paradigmatic instance: moral awareness of gift received + volitional return + physical prostration = a complete conscientious act. Jesus distinguishes this one returning leper from the nine who did not return, suggesting that the wholeness of sōzō is more fully realised in the person who completes the conscientious circuit. Jam 5:15 (vc_id=9024) requires the elders to act with integrated moral awareness (acknowledging sin's possible role), volition (choosing to pray), and action (anointing) — a conscientious process. The characteristic does not impair conscientiousness; in its fullest expressions it *calls conscientiousness forth* as the appropriate inner-being response to sōzō received.
- *T3.10.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The pattern reveals that conscientiousness is an *integrating response-faculty* through which the fullness of sōzō is expressed and confirmed. Where conscientiousness is present (Luk 17:19, Jam 5:15), the healing-wholeness circuit is completed by a person who integrates moral awareness, will, and action in response to what has been received. Where it is absent (the nine lepers, context of Luk 17:19), healing is received but the wholeness-circuit is arguably incomplete — a point Jesus himself marks. This reveals that the characteristic, while activated by faith, finds its fullest human expression in conscientious response: the person who receives sōzō and conscientiously responds to it enters more completely into the inner-being state of wholeness that the characteristic names. Conscientiousness is thus the *completion faculty* of M38-C.
- *T3.11.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if s…_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, centrally. The relational capacity is the structural context within which the entire characteristic operates. Faith in M38-C is always *directed toward a person* (Jesus, God), not toward an impersonal mechanism. The woman seeks Jesus specifically (Mat 9:21, Mar 5:28). Bartimaeus addresses Jesus by name and title (Mar 10:47). The father pleads with Jesus for his daughter (Mar 5:23). The Samaritan returns to give thanks *to Jesus* (Luk 17:19). The prayer of faith in Jam 5:15 is addressed to God. The baptismal appeal in 1Pe 3:21 is "to God." In every case, faith-activated healing is constitutionally relational: the inner faculty of faith is directed toward a relational other (Christ/God), and the outcome (peace, discipleship, forgiven conscience) is a restored or deepened relational standing. The characteristic cannot operate outside the relational axis.
- *T3.11.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic *enables and deepens* relational capacity. The relational outcome of faith-activated healing is consistently a strengthened or newly initiated relationship with Jesus: Bartimaeus "followed Jesus" (Mar 10:52, vc_id=9016) — discipleship as deepened relational engagement; the Samaritan returned to give thanks and was told "your faith has made you well" — relational recognition sealed the wholeness. Peace received (Mar 5:34, Luk 8:48) names a relational state (no longer at enmity or distance, but at rest before Jesus). The baptismal appeal of 1Pe 3:21 is "to God" — establishing a cleared-conscience relational standing before the Father. The characteristic does not impair or bypass relational capacity; it is inherently a relational event, and its deepest effect is the restoration or inauguration of genuine personal connection with Christ and God.
- *T3.11.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The pervasive and consistent engagement of relational capacity across all three VCGs and all twelve verses reveals that this characteristic is *constitutively relational*: it cannot be abstracted from the person-to-person encounter between the faith-seeker and Jesus/God. Faith in M38-C is never generic trust in a principle or force; it is always specifically directed toward a named person (Jesus, "Son of David," God). The characteristic's outcomes (peace, discipleship, cleansed conscience, good standing before God) are all relational states — they describe a changed quality of connection between the person and the divine. The pattern thus reveals that the deepest structure of healing-wholeness through faith exercised is *relational repair and deepening*: physical healing is the visible sign of a relational reality (the person is now in right standing with the source of life), and the wholeness of sōzō is ultimately constituted by the quality of that relational bond. The characteristic's inner-being depth is therefore identical with the depth of relational capacity engaged.
- *T3.2.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, minimally but structurally. The woman's inner speech "if I touch his garment I shall be made well" (Mat 9:21, vc_id=9010) is a conditional proposition — a cognitive inference from knowledge of Jesus to expected outcome. This represents a basic cognitive act: she *understands* something about Jesus that grounds her expectation. Similarly, the father's plea (Mar 5:23, vc_id=9012) implies a cognitive grasp that Jesus can do what physicians cannot. In Jam 5:15 (vc_id=9024) the connection between prayer of faith, healing, and forgiveness requires cognitive integration of physical and spiritual registers. However, the characteristic does not require extended reasoning; the cognitive element is the minimal *belief-content* that anchors faith (a propositional apprehension of Jesus's power), not deliberate theological analysis.
- *T3.2.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic both *enables* minimal cognitive content (the belief-proposition about Jesus's power) and *partially bypasses* extended cognition. Faith in M38-C does not wait for full theological understanding before acting — the woman acts on a conditional inference (Mat 9:21) without a developed christology. Luk 8:50 commands faith precisely when the cognitive data (death of the child) would rationally preclude hope. Jam 5:15 and 1Pe 3:21 require cognitive engagement with the connection between body-healing and conscience-forgiveness, representing a more developed cognitive integration. The characteristic thus *enables* a basic cognitive grasp that grounds faith and *bypasses* the cognitive processing that would counsel despair, while in more mature expressions it *deepens* cognitive integration of physical and spiritual registers.
- *T3.2.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The pattern reveals that this characteristic operates at the *threshold* of cognition: it requires enough cognitive content to be intentional (a belief-proposition about Jesus's power) but is not dependent on extended cognitive processing. The fact that faith precedes Jesus's healing word in most cases (Mat 9:21, Mar 5:28) and is confirmed rather than created by Jesus's statement reveals that the characteristic's cognitive content is *anticipatory and minimal* — a prior grasp that generates expectation rather than a post-hoc interpretation. The bypassing of cognition in Luk 8:50 (faith commanded against the cognitive data of death) further reveals that the characteristic is *supra-cognitive*: it can hold its belief-content against contrary evidence. This distinguishes faith-activated healing from mere rational hope or calculated expectation.
- *T3.3.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Partially and inferentially. The interior convictions operative in M38-C presuppose that the faith-seekers have prior knowledge of Jesus's healing acts or reputation (the woman has heard reports about Jesus — Mark 5:27, background context of vc_id=9013; Bartimaeus calls on the "Son of David," implying remembered messianic expectation). Memory of prior testimony about Jesus functions as the background substrate that makes the interior conviction of M38-C possible. However, the verses themselves do not explicitly name memory as the operative faculty; its role is logically implied rather than textually stated. In 1Pe 3:21 the "resurrection" invoked is a remembered/proclaimed event that grounds the baptismal appeal. The engagement is real but sub-surface.
- *T3.3.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic *enables* the deployment of memorial knowledge of Jesus as background substrate (prior testimony about Jesus recalled by faith-seekers), but the corpus does not evidence memory being deepened, bypassed, or impaired as a distinct consequence of the characteristic. The engagement with memory is enabling and foundational rather than transformative. No verse describes a change in the memory faculty resulting from faith-activated healing.
- *T3.3.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The partial and inferential engagement with memory (T3.3.1, T3.3.2) reveals that this characteristic is *dependent on received testimony* but not primarily a memorial act. The background presence of prior knowledge of Jesus as substrate suggests that faith-activated healing cannot arise ex nihilo — it requires that something has been heard, seen, or told about Jesus that memory holds available. Yet the characteristic's activating moment is not memorial recall but present-tense conviction and action. Memory thus functions as the *enabling precondition* rather than the operative faculty. This reveals that the characteristic stands at the intersection of received testimony (memorial substrate) and present-tense personal faith (operative faculty) — a structure consistent with the broader Pauline "faith comes from hearing" frame, even where that frame is not lexically present in M38-C.
- *T3.4.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, markedly so, especially in VCG-02. Mar 5:23 (vc_id=9012) explicitly glosses the father's inner being as "earnest faith and parental love seeking life" — love and urgency are the affective register driving the plea. Luk 8:50 (vc_id=9018) identifies fear as the affect that Jesus commands faith to displace. In VCG-01, peace received (Mar 5:34, vc_id=9014; Luk 8:48, vc_id=9017) is an affective state marking the inner-being outcome of sōzō — the healing is felt as peace in the soul. Gratitude is noted as an affective response in Luk 17:19 (vc_id=9019, kw: 'gratitude'). Affect is not merely epiphenomenal but is the inner-being climate within which faith is formed and exercised, and peace is the affective seal of the wholeness received.
- *T3.4.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic *transforms* affect: it does not eliminate it but redirects and fulfils it. In VCG-02, fear is not simply bypassed but is actively displaced by faith under command (Luk 8:50, vc_id=9018) — the affect of fear is replaced by the affect of trust. Parental love and urgency (Mar 5:23, vc_id=9012) are not suppressed but are channelled through faith toward a redemptive end. Peace received as outcome (Mar 5:34, Luk 8:48) represents an *enabling and deepening* of positive affect — the soul is brought into a settled affective state of wholeness. Gratitude (Luk 17:19) shows affect *deepened* by the sōzō event. The characteristic does not impair affect; rather, it is the faculty through which distressed affect (fear, grief, urgency) is transformed into restful, grateful affect (peace, discipleship).
- *T3.4.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The pattern of affect engagement across M38-C reveals that this characteristic does not require affective calm as its precondition but can operate through and transform a wide range of affective states. Faith is exercised in conditions of desperation (Mar 5:23), fear (Luk 8:50), chronic suffering (Mar 5:28), marginalisation (Mar 10:46), and leprosy-induced exclusion (Luk 17:19). The characteristic is therefore *affectively robust*: it does not require the person to achieve emotional equilibrium before faith becomes possible. Rather, the distressed affective state becomes the occasion for faith's exercise, and peace/gratitude is the affective transformation that follows sōzō. This reveals that the characteristic bridges the most extreme negative affective states (mortal fear, chronic anguish) and the most positive (peace, wholeness), with faith as the interior faculty that makes the transit.
- *T3.6.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, and volition is structurally central. Faith in M38-C is not passive reception but an active choice to press through a crowd (Mar 5:27–28, context vc_id=9013), to call out persistently against social opposition (Mar 10:47–48, context vc_id=9016), to make a desperate plea (Mar 5:23, vc_id=9012), to return and give thanks (Luk 17:15–16, context vc_id=9019), and to offer intercessory prayer (Jam 5:15, vc_id=9024). Each of these is a volitional act — a determined choice to pursue the sōzō object. Luk 8:50 (vc_id=9018) is the sharpest instance: Jesus commands "only believe" — faith is here a volitional response to a command, placing volition at the cusp between divine imperative and human choice. The characteristic cannot be separated from the will's engagement.
- *T3.6.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with …_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic *enables and strengthens* volition. The evidence shows willpower actively engaged and carried through against obstacles: the woman presses through a crowd despite her ritual uncleanness (Mar 5:28); Bartimaeus continues crying out despite being silenced by the crowd (Mar 10:47–48, context vc_id=9016); the father pleads on behalf of another person with urgent determination (Mar 5:23). Luk 8:50 commands volition ("only believe") as a counter-act to fear — here the characteristic directly addresses the volitional capacity, commanding it to override an emotionally compelling alternative. Faith as presented in M38-C does not bypass the will (it is not imposed) but *strengthens* it — the person's will is fully engaged and its exercise is the activating mechanism of the sōzō event. No evidence of impairment.
- *T3.6.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The consistent and strong engagement of volition across all three VCGs reveals that faith-activated healing-wholeness is *constitutively volitional*: it cannot occur without the person's determined exercise of will. This is theologically significant: the characteristic does not represent a passive divine imposition but a genuine human willing-toward-God that is confirmed and honoured by divine response. The fact that Jesus attributes causation to the person's faith ("your faith has made you well") rather than to his own sovereign act reveals that the volitional structure of the characteristic is not incidental but definitional. Simultaneously, the command "only believe" (Luk 8:50) shows that volition is addressable and commandable — it is not self-generated absolutely but can be evoked by authoritative word. The pattern reveals a *commanded-yet-genuine* volition: real human choice operating in response to divine invitation.
- *T3.7.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, strongly. The agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — is extensively engaged. The woman initiates the approach and touch (Mat 9:21, vc_id=9010; Mar 5:28, vc_id=9013). Bartimaeus initiates and persists in his cry (Mar 10:52, vc_id=9016). The father makes an urgent plea (Mar 5:23, vc_id=9012). The Samaritan turns back and prostrates himself (Luk 17:19, vc_id=9019). The elders anoint and pray (Jam 5:15, vc_id=9024). The baptismal candidate makes an "appeal to God" (1Pe 3:21, vc_id=8992). In every case the faith-seeker is an active agent initiating or completing a directed act toward Jesus/God. Jesus's confirmation formula ("your faith has made you well") retroactively identifies the person's agency as the humanly operative cause — not passive waiting but directed initiative.
- *T3.7.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic strongly *enables* agency. As noted in T3.7.1, every instance in M38-C involves the faith-seeker as an active initiator. Jesus's confirmation formula ("your faith has made you well") *deepens* the person's sense of agency retroactively — they are told that their inner act was causally operative in the healing. This divine confirmation of human agency is remarkable: Jesus does not say "I healed you" but "your faith has saved you," attributing causation to the person's inner faculty. This deepens rather than overrides human agency, presenting the characteristic as one that elevates the person's inner-being capacity to be a genuine secondary cause in the sōzō event. No bypassing or impairment of agency is evidenced.
- *T3.7.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The pattern of consistent, strong, and divinely-affirmed agency engagement across M38-C reveals that this characteristic exemplifies a distinctive biblical anthropology: human inner-being agency is genuinely operative as a secondary cause within a divinely-effected event. Jesus's repeated attribution formula establishes that the person's inner-being act (faith exercised) is the named human mechanism through which divine saving power flows. This is not a diminution of divine sovereignty (sōzō is always ultimately God's act) but an elevation of human agency: the person is constitutionally capable of directing an inner-being faculty in such a way that it becomes the receiving and activating conduit of divine wholeness. The pattern reveals that the characteristic is *co-agential* — divine and human agency operating in structured complementarity, with faith as the hinge.
- *T3.8.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — a…_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Partially. Moral evaluation is not the primary faculty operative in the individual synoptic healings of VCG-01 and VCG-02, where the presenting need is physical. However, VCG-03 introduces a moral evaluation dimension: Jam 5:15 (vc_id=9024) states "if he has committed sins, he will be forgiven," implying that the person must have moral awareness of sin for forgiveness to be relevant. 1Pe 3:21 (vc_id=8992) grounds the saving appeal in the desire for "a good conscience" — conscience being the organ of moral self-evaluation before God. The characteristic thus engages moral evaluation specifically at the point where physical healing opens onto spiritual forgiveness: the person's inner being must be capable of recognising moral standing as a dimension of the wholeness sought.
- *T3.8.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic *deepens* moral evaluation at the point where physical healing opens onto spiritual forgiveness. Jam 5:15 (vc_id=9024) — "if he has committed sins, he will be forgiven" — invites the sick person and the praying elders to hold open the possibility that sin has contributed to illness, requiring moral self-evaluation. 1Pe 3:21 (vc_id=8992) grounds the saving appeal in the desire for "a good conscience" — meaning that the person has evaluated their conscience before God and desires it to be cleared. The characteristic does not impair or bypass moral evaluation; rather, the wholeness it delivers is partly constituted by the fulfilment of moral evaluation (conscience satisfied, sin forgiven). No bypassing or impairment is evidenced.
- *T3.8.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The partial engagement with moral evaluation — present in VCG-03 but largely absent from VCG-01 and VCG-02 — reveals that moral evaluation is not the *activating* faculty of this characteristic but its *deepening* faculty. The individual synoptic healings do not require the faith-seeker to evaluate their moral standing before faith can be exercised — faith is directed at physical healing, and the spiritual register is implied or supplementary. In Jam 5:15 and 1Pe 3:21, the characteristic's reach has expanded to explicitly include moral evaluation as part of the wholeness sought. The pattern thus reveals a developmental structure: the characteristic begins (in VCG-01/02) as faith-toward-physical-healing with spiritual overtone, and matures (in VCG-03) into a faith that explicitly addresses moral standing. Moral evaluation is the endpoint-deepening of the characteristic, not its starting point.
- *T3.9.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — Yes, explicitly and definitionally in VCG-03. 1Pe 3:21 (vc_id=8992) is the clearest instance: baptism saves "as an appeal to God for a good conscience through the resurrection of Jesus Christ" — conscience is the named inner organ that salvation addresses and clears. The meaning gloss states: "salvation touches and clears the conscience before God." Jam 5:15 (vc_id=9024) pairs healing and forgiveness, with the body-and-conscience pairing establishing that the sōzō event in this characteristic reaches the conscience as its spiritual terminus. In VCG-01 and VCG-02 the conscience is not explicitly named, but the "peace" received (Mar 5:34, Luk 8:48) can be read as a conscience-state — the inner being no longer alienated but at rest before God. The conscience is definitively engaged at the characteristic's deepest reach.
- *T3.9.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The characteristic *enables and clears* the conscience. In 1Pe 3:21 (vc_id=8992) the saving event is specifically the restoration of a good conscience — sōzō reaches its inner terminus in conscience-cleansing. In Jam 5:15 (vc_id=9024) forgiveness accompanies healing, meaning the conscience that was burdened by sin is released. The characteristic thus *enables* a good conscience to exist where a troubled one did before. There is no evidence of the characteristic impairing or bypassing conscience; rather, conscience is the deepest stratum that the sōzō event must reach for healing-wholeness to be complete. Peace granted (Mar 5:34, Luk 8:48) may be understood as a conscience at rest, further supporting this pattern.
- *T3.9.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** E — The pattern reveals that conscience is the *ultimate inner-being terminus* of this characteristic. In VCG-01 and VCG-02 the conscience is implicitly addressed through peace (Mar 5:34, Luk 8:48) but not named. In VCG-03 (1Pe 3:21, Jam 5:15) it is explicitly named as the inner organ that sōzō clears and restores. This progressive revelation — from implied peace (soul at rest) to explicitly cleared conscience — reveals that healing-wholeness in M38-C is not complete at the physical level but has a necessary inner-being terminus in conscience-restoration. The pattern further reveals that faith-activated wholeness is not merely therapeutic (body restored) but forensic and relational (conscience cleared before God). The full characteristic is not present unless conscience is reached. The non-engagement of conscience in VCG-01 and VCG-02 does not contradict this; rather, the peace granted in those texts is the experiential form of the conscience-at-rest that VCG-03 names explicitly.

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.5.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — The corpus does not evidence engagement of the creative faculty (imagination, origination) as a distinct operative element in faith-activated healing-wholeness. The woman's interior conviction is better characterised as perception and trust than as imagination. No verse in M38-C invokes the creative capacity of the inner being. This faculty appears to be silent here.
- *T3.5.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — The corpus is silent on any enabling, deepening, bypassing, or impairing of the creative faculty through faith-activated healing-wholeness. No evidence in M38-C addresses this relationship.
- *T3.5.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-3]** S — The consistent non-engagement with the creative faculty across M38-C reveals that this characteristic does not require or produce imaginative origination as part of its operation. The inner-being faculty engaged is trust directed toward a known person (Jesus/God), not the generative production of new inner-being content. This silence reveals that faith-activated healing-wholeness is a *receptive and relational* characteristic rather than an originating or creative one — it receives and trusts rather than imagines and creates.

**Key verses for Healing wholeness through faith exercised:**

**Mat 9:22** (G4982 sōzō) [M38-C-VCG-01]
> Mat 9:22 Jesus turned , and seeing her he said , “Take heart , daughter ; your faith has made you well .” And instantly the woman was made well .
_Meaning of the term here:_ Jesus confirms healing through faith — 'your faith has made you well' — the sōzō is healing with spiritual resonance, with faith as the inner-being faculty that activates the saving act.

**Luk 8:50** (G4982 sōzō) [M38-C-VCG-02]
> Luk 8:50 But Jesus on hearing this answered him , “Do not fear ; only believe , and she will be well .”
_Meaning of the term here:_ Jesus counters fear with the command to believe so that the girl will be made well — sōzō names physical rescue from death, with faith explicitly set against fear as the inner faculty that opens the door to saving action.

**Jam 5:15** (G4982 sōzō) [M38-C-VCG-03]
> Jam 5:15 And the prayer of faith will save the one who is sick , and the Lord will raise him up . And if he has committed sins , he will be forgiven .
_Meaning of the term here:_ The prayer of faith heals the sick and secures forgiveness if there is sin; healing and spiritual salvation converge — the inner being is restored in body and conscience through interceding faith.

**T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries**

- *T2.10.1* — _Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other direction…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — There is partial evidence of constitutional movement. Lev 17:11 (VCG-02) shows movement from blood (body/physical medium) to soul-covering. The Levitical ritual complex (VCG-01) involves body-actions (animal sacrifice, priest's hand, altar blood) producing soul/conscience-level outcomes (forgiveness, guilt removed). Isa 6:7 (VCG-04) shows body-touch (lip/coal) producing inner-being transformation. The direction is consistently from external physical act through divine acceptance to inner conscience-clearing — body to soul, mediated by divine action. No explicit spirit-level terminus is named.
- *T2.10.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The sequence evidenced is: (1) external physical action (sacrifice, blood, coal-touch, hand-laying) → (2) divine acceptance/declaration → (3) inner-being conscience-clearing/forgiveness. This is a consistent three-stage pattern across VCG-01 through VCG-05. The movement runs from external-physical through divine mediation to inner-soul, not the reverse. VCG-06 (negative pole) confirms the pattern by negation: when the mechanism is blocked (1Sa 3:14, Isa 22:14), the inner-being remains burdened with guilt — no inner-being movement occurs without the prior stages completing. The pattern is irreversible in direction: outer-to-inner via divine action.
- *T2.10.3* — _If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Constitutional movement is evidenced (see obs_id=288–289). The pattern runs external-physical → divine acceptance → inner conscience-clearing. Silence-note does not apply. The movement is outer-to-inner via divine action and is consistently directed from body/ritual through divine declaration to soul-level transformation.
- *T2.2.1* — _Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Lev 17:11 (M38-D-VCG-02) most directly names the soul as the locus: "blood on the altar makes atonement for the soul (nepeš)." The atonement mechanism is explicitly soul-targeted — life substituted for life, covering provided for the soul. Exo 30:15–16 reinforces this with ransom-language for "every life" (nepeš), placing atonement at the soul-level as a universal requirement. The psalmist's relief in Psa 65:3 ("iniquities overwhelm me, you atone for them") also implies the inner personal self as the site of both burden and release.
- *T2.2.2* — _What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Lev 17:11's explicit "blood atones for the soul (nepeš)" establishes that atonement-received is directed at the deepest seat of personal life — the animating, living self. The soul as the locus means this characteristic addresses the most fundamental layer of personal existence before God, not merely external standing or behavioral modification. The soul's condition — burdened by guilt or freed through covering — is the ultimate object of the atonement mechanism. This positions conscience-cleansed atonement as intrinsically personal and existential rather than merely ceremonial.
- *T2.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence is not silent; soul-level location is explicitly evidenced. Lev 17:11 names the soul (nepeš) directly as the target of atonement. Exo 30:15–16 names each person's nepeš as requiring equal ransom-covering. The characteristic is definitively a soul-level phenomenon in this corpus. Noting this finding as positive, not silent.
- *T2.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Partially. Pro 16:6 ("iniquity atoned through steadfast love and faithfulness; fear of the LORD turns from evil") places atonement in proximity to moral orientation and the will — capacities associated with the heart — though the heart (lēb) is not named explicitly. 2Ch 30:18 (M38-D-VCG-03) involves Hezekiah's intercession for those whose "heart was set to seek God" even if ritually unprepared, implying that heart-sincerity is a relevant condition for atonement-received. The evidence is indirect but present.
- *T2.3.2* — _What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The indirect heart-evidence (2Ch 30:18; Pro 16:6) suggests that atonement-received engages the heart primarily through its moral awareness and relational-orientation functions. In 2Ch 30:18, the "heart set to seek God" is the qualifying condition for receiving atonement even under ritual irregularity — the heart's directedness toward God is the operative factor. Pro 16:6 connects atonement to the moral transformation axis (fear of LORD, turning from evil), implicating the heart's willing and moral-evaluating capacities. The heart's integrating function engaged is the alignment of will and moral awareness toward God as the condition for and response to atonement.
- *T2.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence is not entirely silent, but explicit heart-location is indirect. The heart (lēb) is not named as the explicit site of atonement-received in any verse. The heart-proximate evidence (2Ch 30:18 — heart's directedness; Pro 16:6 — moral transformation connected to atonement) is present but not a direct heart-location claim. Noting: the evidence is indirect and limited; the characteristic is not explicitly located in the heart by the corpus.
- *T2.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence surface any soul-level location beyond heart and mind for this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Yes. The conscience emerges as the functionally described soul-subset most consistently engaged. Across M38-D-VCG-01 (Lev 4:20, 26, 31, 35; 5:6, 10, 13, 16, 18; 6:7; 19:22), the keyword "conscience cleansed" recurs as the definitive inner-being outcome, even though the Hebrew does not use a term for "conscience" directly. The movement from sin-burdened to forgiven-and-at-peace names a conscience-level state. Isa 6:7 (M38-D-VCG-04) describes guilt specifically as removed from lips — a body-proximate expression of the inner conscience-state.
- *T2.5.2* — _If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The conscience-layer is the functionally described soul-subset most consistently operative. The recurrent keyword "conscience cleansed" across M38-D-VCG-01 and the explicit description of guilt being "removed" (Isa 6:7: "your guilt is taken away") points to the conscience as the specific inner register where atonement-received is experienced. Luk 18:13 (VCG-05) — the tax collector's "be merciful to me, a sinner" from a posture of beaten-chest contrition — names the conscience-level experience of sin-awareness and its plea for relief. This reveals that conscience is the seat of the characteristic's operation: the place where guilt accumulates and where covering is received as relief.
- *T2.5.3* — _If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence is not silent. As noted in obs_id=273 and obs_id=274, the conscience-layer is evidenced as the operative soul-subset beyond heart and mind. The corpus surfaces it through functional description (guilt removed, cleansed, relieved) rather than explicit anatomical naming, but the convergence of keywords ("conscience cleansed," "guilt removed," "sin-laden resolved") across VCG-01 and VCG-04 is sufficient to identify conscience as a distinct soul-subset location.
- *T2.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Yes, partially. Isa 6:7 (M38-D-VCG-04) links atonement to the lips specifically: the burning coal touches Isaiah's lips and the declaration follows — "your guilt is taken away, your sin atoned for." The lips as site of uncleanness (Isa 6:5) become the site of cleansing. Lev 4–6 (M38-D-VCG-01) connects atonement to the physical act of hand-laying on the sacrifice (Lev 1:4, VCG-02), where the body-gesture of the hand enacts the substitutionary transfer. Blood is the physical medium across VCG-02 (Lev 17:11).
- *T2.6.2* — _If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Scripture's body-links in this characteristic function as mediating and expressive. In Isa 6:7, the lip-touch is both expressive (the lips were the site of declared unworthiness: "I am a man of unclean lips") and mediating (the physical touch enacts the inner-being transformation declared immediately after). In Lev 1:4 (VCG-02), hand-laying on the sacrifice is performatively mediating — the gesture effects the identification-transfer that grounds the atonement. The body is not incidental; it is the enacted surface through which the inner-being reality of guilt-transfer and covering is ritually realized. Scripture uses the body as a necessary conduit for the inner-being state change.
- *T2.6.3* — _If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Body-part links are evidenced (Isa 6:7 — lips; Lev 1:4 — hand; Lev 17:11 — blood as the body's life-substance). This prompt's condition ("if no body-part link") does not apply. The links are present and have been analyzed in obs_id=276–280.
- *T2.7.1* — _Where a body-characteristic link exists, which direction does it run — does the soul express through the body, does the body feed back to th…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The directionality is primarily soul-to-body-expressing and body-mediating-to-soul. In Lev 1:4 (M38-D-VCG-02), the worshipper's hand-laying is a bodily gesture that expresses the inner identification with the sacrifice and simultaneously enacts the soul-level transfer. In Isa 6:7, the coal touches the body (lips), but the declared result is inner-being transformation (guilt removed, sin atoned). The body serves as the mediating surface through which atonement's inner-being effect is both enacted and proclaimed — neither purely expressive nor purely causal, but genuinely mediating.
- *T2.7.2* — _What is the consequence of that directionality for understanding the characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The body-mediating direction means atonement-received is not a purely spiritual or cognitive event but one that requires enacted, embodied participation. The consequence is that this characteristic has an inherently incarnational structure: the covering of the soul is achieved through physical sacrifice (blood), physical gesture (hand-laying), and physical touch (coal on lips). This prevents atonement-received from being reduced to mental assent or emotional feeling; it is grounded in bodily reality. In NT terms (Rom 3:25, Heb 2:17), Christ's bodily death as hilastērios continues this mediating direction — physical enactment produces inner-being soul-covering.
- *T2.7.3* — _If no body-characteristic link is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Body-characteristic links are evidenced, so this silence-note does not apply. The directionality has been analyzed (obs_id=279–280): the body functions as a mediating surface through which the inner-being conscience-clearing is enacted and declared. The finding stands positive.
- *T2.9.1* — _Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, …_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence presents a dominant pattern of external, divine origination. M38-D-VCG-04 is the most explicit: Psa 65:3 ("God himself atones"), Psa 78:38 ("God's compassion led him to atone"), 1Jo 4:10 ("God sent his Son as propitiation — his love, not human initiative"). Lev 17:11 states God himself provides the blood mechanism: "I have given it for you." Even the Levitical system (VCG-01) is divinely instituted — the priest mediates but the covering is God-ordained. The one verse with human moral contribution (Pro 16:6, "steadfast love and faithfulness") represents a participatory dimension, but VCG-04 and VCG-05 collectively establish that the originating source is divine gift.
- *T2.9.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — The evidence reveals a primary singular divine source with a secondary participatory human dimension. The singular divine source is dominant: VCG-04 (Psa 65:3, Psa 78:38, 1Jo 4:10) consistently names God as the originating agent who provides, initiates, and gives the covering. VCG-05 (Rom 3:25) names Christ as the divinely set-forth mechanism "received by faith" — human faith is the mode of reception, not the source of origination. The participatory human dimension (sacrifice brought, hand laid, prayer offered) appears across VCG-01, VCG-02, VCG-03, but in each case the human act is responsive to and dependent upon the divinely ordained system. The origin is singular (divine) with multiple modes of human reception.
- *T2.9.3* — _Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** E — Yes, with important nuance. In the Levitical priestly context (VCG-01, VCG-02), the originating source is the divinely instituted sacrificial system mediated by a human priest — God's mechanism is operative but a human agent is required. In the Davidic/royal intercessory context (VCG-03: 2Sa 21:3, 2Ch 30:18), the mechanism shifts to prayer and royal intercession. In VCG-04 (divine initiative texts: Psa 65:3, Psa 78:38, 1Jo 4:10), origination is purely divine with no human mediation. In VCG-05 (NT propitiation), the mechanism is Christ's once-for-all self-offering received by faith. The origin is consistently divine but the mediation-mode changes: priest → king/intercessor → God directly → Christ. The shift across contexts shows a progressive narrowing toward unmediated divine initiative.

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch4 — T2 silences for Conscience cleansed through atonement received -->

**T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries**

- *T2.1.1* — _Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — The verse evidence across all seven VCGs does not explicitly use "spirit" (rûaḥ or pneuma) as the locus of atonement-received. The inner-being language is consistently that of guilt-removal, forgiveness, covering, and conscience-clearing, but no verse in this corpus names the spirit-level as the explicit site.
- *T2.1.2* — _Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — The evidence does not identify this characteristic as originating at or primarily inhabiting the spirit level. Origination is consistently located in divine agency (God gives, God sends, God atones) and is received at the soul/conscience level. The spirit (rûaḥ/pneuma) is not named as a relevant constitutional register in this corpus.
- *T2.1.3* — _What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. No verse in this corpus names the spirit (rûaḥ/pneuma) as the site of atonement-received. Any inference about spirit-level depth would be speculative relative to this corpus. The characteristic's depth is evidenced at the soul/conscience level (Lev 17:11; Luk 18:13) rather than explicitly at the spirit level.
- *T2.1.4* — _If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — The evidence is silent on spirit-level location. No verse in this corpus — across all seven VCGs spanning Leviticus, Psalms, Isaiah, Ezekiel, Daniel, Luke, Romans, Hebrews, and 1 John — names the spirit (rûaḥ or pneuma) as the site, origin, or register of atonement-received. This silence is consistent and not incidental. The characteristic is evidenced exclusively at the soul/conscience level.
- *T2.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — No verse in this corpus explicitly names the mind (nous or bîn-faculty) as the site of atonement-received. The characteristic's inner-being movement is presented in terms of guilt/conscience, standing before God, and relational status rather than cognitive understanding.
- *T2.4.2* — _What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — The evidence is silent on mind-level engagement for this characteristic. No verse in the corpus locates atonement-received in the mind's knowing, discerning, or understanding function. The characteristic operates at the conscience/guilt level rather than the cognitive-rational level.
- *T2.4.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mind-location, note this explicitly._
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — The evidence is silent on mind-location for this characteristic. No verse in this corpus names or implies the mind (nous, śēkel, or bîn-faculty) as the site or register of atonement-received. The characteristic operates at the conscience/guilt/soul level without reference to cognitive-mental function.
- *T2.8.1* — _Does sustained operation of this characteristic leave a constitutional deposit in the body or its design — including DNA or generational con…_
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — The verse evidence is silent on atonement-received leaving a constitutional deposit in the body, DNA, or generational physiology. Generational guilt is addressed (e.g., Deu 21:8 covering corporate blood-guilt; Dan 9:24 eschatological iniquity-covering), but this is presented as communal/covenantal standing rather than bodily deposit. No verse describes a somatic legacy of conscience-cleansed atonement.
- *T2.8.2* — _What evidence supports or contradicts this?_
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — No evidence in this corpus supports or contradicts the idea of a somatic constitutional deposit from sustained atonement-received. The characteristic is presented as event-based (forgiveness at a specific moment) or ongoing relational status (Exo 30:16, kept in divine remembrance), but no verse describes this producing a lasting change in bodily constitution. The corporate/generational dimension (Deu 21:8, Dan 9:24) pertains to covenantal standing, not bodily deposit. This finding feeds directly into T5.7.
- *T2.8.3* — _If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly. This finding feeds directly into T5.7._
  → **[CHAR-4]** S — The evidence is silent on any bodily constitutional deposit from atonement-received. No verse in this corpus describes a lasting somatic change, generational bodily consequence, or DNA-level legacy from conscience-cleansed atonement. The characteristic produces inner-being relational status change (forgiven, covered, guilt-removed) without evidenced somatic deposit. This finding feeds directly into T5.7.
